{"nick":"joepie91","message":"ttal: so the *wrong* way to sign applications, is to do the signing on that very server that is easy to compromise, because it means the signing keys have to be on there, which means that anybody compromising the server can just sign their backdoored version, which defeats the point of application signing","date":"2017-06-30T23:45:55.314Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"ttal: however, if you sign locally (ie. not on the download server), an attacker would have to compromise *two* systems (the download server *and* your local system), the latter of which is not that easy to get into","date":"2017-06-30T23:46:21.237Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"this makes compromising people through maliciously modified updates much, much harder","date":"2017-06-30T23:46:32.655Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"to the point of \"don't bother\" for most attackers","date":"2017-06-30T23:46:37.774Z","type":"message"}
